public class Conditions {
public static void main(String args[]) {
Scanner sc = new Scanner(System.in);
int a = sc.nextInt();
int b = sc.nextInt();
int operator = sc.nextInt();


/**
* 1 -> +
* 2 -> -
* 3 -> *
* 4 -> /
* 5 -> %
*/


switch(operator) {
case 1 : System.out.println(a+b);
break;
case 2 : System.out.println(a-b);
break;
case 3 : System.out.println(a*b);
break;
case 4 : if(b == 0) {
System.out.println("Invalid Division");
} else {
System.out.println(a/b);
}
break;
case 5 : if(b == 0) {
System.out.println("Invalid Division");
} else {
System.out.println(a%b);
}
break;
default : System.out.println("Invalid Operator");
}
} Bara ja SSD lagalo

🙂🙂🥲🥲 Ooo ta ke Mane triyasha k 🥲🥲🥲 😂😂😂😂😂😂 Na dat kaliye,line a aso 😇🙂🫣 Ara khawabo re 🥲🥲 dekh bara ki rokom rag lage bal kono lom problem nai bara tao thikmoto run hocche na bara 😶😶😶😶 Intellij te dekh duto te eee bara bal
eirokom bar bar hole kar iccha kore bol 😶😶😶 Setai java r pod ee giye bas dhukate iccha korcche lom 😶😶😶 Hm 😂 import java.util.Scanner;

public class NumberPyramid {
public static void main(String[] args) {
Scanner scanner = new Scanner(System.in);
System.out.print("Enter the number of rows: ");
int rows = scanner.nextInt();

for (int i = 1; i <= rows; i++) {
// Print spaces
for (int j = 1; j <= rows - i; j++) {
System.out.print(" ");
}

// Print numbers in ascending order
for (int j = 1; j <= i; j++) {
System.out.print(j);
}

// Print numbers in descending order
for (int j = i - 1; j >= 1; j--) {
System.out.print(j);
}

System.out.println(); // Move to the next line for the next row
}

scanner.close();
}
} vai sera rogor hoyecche 😂😂😂😂😂😂😂😂😂😂😂😂😂😂😂😂😂😂 ai meye ta re vai

Bol🙂 Ara bara kalke game khelchilam oi jonno ☠️☠️ Hmm ☠️☠️☠️☠️ Hm ☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️ Hmm In a DC (direct current) motor, the back electromotive force (back EMF) plays a crucial role in the motor's operation. Back EMF is generated when the armature of the motor rotates within the magnetic field produced by the stator. This phenomenon is based on Faraday's law of electromagnetic induction, which states that a changing magnetic field induces an electromotive force (EMF) in a conductor.

Here's the significance of back EMF in a DC motor:

1. **Counter-electromotive force (Counter-EMF):** Back EMF acts as a counter-electromotive force against the applied voltage. As the motor spins, the back EMF opposes the flow of current through the armature windings. This opposition is beneficial because it limits the current flowing through the motor. Without back EMF, the motor could draw excessive current, leading to overheating and potential damage.

2. **Current Regulation:** Back EMF helps regulate the current in the motor. As the speed of the motor increases, the magnitude of the back EMF also increases. This rise in back EMF effectively reduces the net voltage across the armature, limiting the current. Conversely, at lower speeds, the back EMF is lower, allowing more current to flow, which is necessary to overcome the initial inertia and start the motor.

3. **Energy Efficiency:** Back EMF contributes to the energy efficiency of the motor. By opposing the applied voltage, it prevents the motor from drawing excessive current, reducing power losses and heat dissipation. This makes the DC motor more efficient in converting electrical energy into mechanical energy.

4. **Dynamic Braking:** Back EMF is utilized in dynamic braking systems. When the motor is decelerating or needs to stop quickly, the power supply to the motor is disconnected, allowing the motor to act as a generator. The back EMF generated during this process helps dissipate the kinetic energy of the rotating armature, effectively slowing down the motor.

In summary, the significance of back EMF in a DC motor lies in its role as a self-regulating mechanism that helps control current, enhances energy efficiency, and facilitates dynamic braking. Understanding and leveraging the effects of back EMF are crucial for designing and operating DC motors efficiently and safely. The back electromotive force (EMF) in a DC motor is the voltage induced in the armature winding due to the rotation of the armature in the magnetic field. It opposes the applied voltage and is denoted by Eb. The significance of back EMF in a DC motor is that it makes the motor a self-regulating machine, causing it to draw only the amount of armature current needed to develop the required torque. When the motor is running at no load, the back EMF is nearly equal to the applied voltage, resulting in a small armature current. However, when a load is connected, the back EMF decreases, causing a larger armature current to flow, which in turn increases the torque. This self-regulating behavior is essential for the efficient and controlled operation of DC motors[1][2].

The back EMF is crucial in limiting the armature current, which in turn affects the motor's speed and torque. It plays a significant role in the energy conversion process within the motor, as it limits the armature current to the level required for the desired torque, thus enabling efficient operation and preventing excessive power consumption[1][2].

Citations: To calculate the core loss current, magnetizing current, and iron loss in the distribution transformer, we can use the following formulas:

1. **Apparent Power (S):** \(S = V_{\text{primary}} \times I_{\text{no-load}}\)
2. **Active Power (P):** \(P = S \times \text{Power factor}\)
3. **Reactive Power (Q):** \(Q = S \times \sqrt{1 - \text{Power factor}^2}\)
4. **Magnetizing Reactance (Xm):** \(Xm = \frac{V_{\text{primary}}}{I_{\text{no-load}} \times \sqrt{1 - \text{Power factor}^2}}\)
5. **Magnetizing Current (Im):** \(Im = \frac{V_{\text{primary}}}{Xm}\)
6. **Iron Loss (Pi):** \(Pi = P - \text{Active Power consumed by the core}\)
7. **Core Loss Current (Ic):** \(Ic = \frac{Pi}{V_{\text{primary}} \times \text{Power factor}}\)

Given:
- \(V_{\text{primary}} = 11 \ kV = 11000 \ V\)
- \(V_{\text{secondary}} = 400 \ V\)
- \(I_{\text{no-load}} = 1 \ A\)
- Power factor \(= 0.24\) (lagging)

Let's calculate step by step:

1. **Apparent Power (S):**
\[ S = 11000 \ V \times 1 \ A = 11000 \ VA \]

2. **Active Power (P):**
\[ P = 11000 \ VA \times 0.24 = 2640 \ W \]

3. **Reactive Power (Q):**
\[ Q = 11000 \ VA \times \sqrt{1 - 0.24^2} = 10746 \ VAR \]

4. **Magnetizing Reactance (Xm):**
\[ Xm = \frac{11000 \ V}{1 \ A \times \sqrt{1 - 0.24^2}} \approx 11444 \ \Omega \]

5. **Magnetizing Current (Im):**
\[ Im = \frac{11000 \ V}{11444 \ \Omega} \approx 0.96 \ A \]

6. **Iron Loss (Pi):**
\[ Pi = 2640 \ W - \text{Active Power consumed by the core} \]

7. **Core Loss Current (Ic):**
\[ Ic = \frac{Pi}{11000 \ V \times 0.24} \]

Now, you can substitute the values into the equations to find the results. Suye ga6is naki? Amar ex bou status deya st korlo naki??..🐻

abar bara amar bou k tanar ki holo ☠️☠️☠️ Patla tai Oi bol As6is? hmmm barite acchi 100g misti chanachur niye asis please 🙏🙂 Niche kauke na dekhiye upore niye asis ☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️ Please 🙂 ☠️☠️☠️☠️☠️ Niye ai 20 takar Gand fata similarity 🥲 In English pronunciation, monophthongs are single, pure vowel sounds that do not involve a change in quality during their production. Central monophthongs are those vowels produced with the tongue positioned towards the center of the mouth. In the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA), central monophthongs are represented by symbols that indicate their specific articulation. Here are some central monophthongs in English:

1. **/ə/ - Schwa:**
- The schwa is a very short, neutral vowel sound. It is the most central and unstressed vowel in English. It is found in unstressed syllables, such as the first syllable of "banana."

2. **/ɜː/ - Open-mid central unrounded:**
- This sound is found in words like "bird" or "herd." The tongue is in a mid-open position, and the lips are unrounded.

3. **/ʌ/ - Open-mid back unrounded:**
- This sound is heard in words like "cup" or "luck." The tongue is in a mid-open position, and it is positioned towards the back of the mouth.

4. **/ɐ/ - Near-open central:**
- This sound is less common in standard English but can be found in some accents. It is similar to the schwa but is slightly more open. An example might be the first syllable in "sofa" in some accents.

It's important to note that the exact realization of these sounds can vary depending on factors such as accent, dialect, and surrounding sounds. Understanding these central monophthongs is crucial for accurate pronunciation and phonetic analysis in English. It simplifies the comparison of algorithm efficiency by focusing on growth rates while ignoring constant factors and lower-order terms.

import mediapipe as mp
import time

# Initialize Pose model from Mediapipe
mp_pose = mp.solutions.pose
pose = mp_pose.Pose()

cap = cv2.VideoCapture('motionvideo1.mp4')

# Resize window
cv2.namedWindow("Image", cv2.WINDOW_NORMAL)
cv2.resizeWindow("Image", 640, 480)

previous_time = 0

while True:
success, img = cap.read()
if not success:
break

imgRGB = cv2.cvtColor(img, cv2.COLOR_BGR2RGB)
results = pose.process(imgRGB)

# Check if pose landmarks are detected
if results.pose_landmarks:
for landmark in results.pose_landmarks.landmark:
# Process landmarks as needed
pass

# FPS measurement
current_time = time.time()
fps = 1 / (current_time - previous_time)
previous_time = current_time

# Display FPS on the image
cv2.putText(img, str(int(fps)), (70, 50), cv2.FONT_HERSHEY_COMPLEX, 1, (255, 0, 0), 3)

cv2.imshow("Image", img)
if cv2.waitKey(1) & 0xFF == ord('q'):
break

cap.release()
cv2.destroyAllWindows() null Subject python

Tui nije mukh fute bolechilis 👀 kobe bara mone nai 👀 from datasets import load_dataset

# Choose your dataset
dataset_name = "Skylion007/openwebtext"
split = "train"

# Load the dataset
dataset = load_dataset(dataset_name, split=split)

# Optional: Save full dataset to text file (raw)
with open("huggingface_dataset.txt", "w", encoding="utf-8") as f:
for item in dataset:
f.write(item['text'] + "\n")

# Split into 90% train, 10% val
split_dataset = dataset.train_test_split(test_size=0.1, seed=42)

# Save split datasets as text files
with open("train.txt", "w", encoding="utf-8") as train_file:
for item in split_dataset['train']:
train_file.write(item['text'] + "\n")

with open("val.txt", "w", encoding="utf-8") as val_file:
for item in split_dataset['test']:
val_file.write(item['text'] + "\n")

print("✅ Dataset downloaded, split into train.txt (90%) and val.txt (10%)") Oii Dher bal suyeu porlo kane ki hoise Bad de toder class jai automata r brive er like ta diyecche ota share kor amake Ppt r? huu ore khanki toder ekta drive j sob ppt upload hoyecche ota de eta na Etai diyechilo ara seta na toder sobar ppt gulo dekhbo oi jonno Janina ar bara Bujhechi 🐧 200 korte bol kiser jonno ? or kache r online nai bollo vorte hobe tarpor De na jogar kore 200 ontoto Taratari nai re pai nai null call korli kan College jacchis naki hmm kano ?
